I looked at the page where that photo came from, and they said nothing about it glowing. Because of the crackled glass and the flash from the camera (that much is apparent from the shadow under the marble) light reflected and made it appear like it was glowing. Nothing more, and no photoshop. Just a trick of the light reflecting on the crackle from the camera flash. And next time, don't be such a newb. Use gloves.

Oook that was obvious. Marbles with colors and swirls inside are not uniform as the single colors are, so they snap there. Also raising temp was risky, you should wait more time, else glass can explode
Finished trying this out with some flat glass gems, and I can say it probably works better with flats than with round marbles. I put 22 gems of many sizes and varieties of colors in the oven at 500Â°F for 20 minutes than gently tipped them into the ice bath. Here are a few observations on the final results:  -This works just as well for darker glasses, but might be better if used for a suncatcher or stained glass project.Â   -The lighter colors show more of the cracked glass if you put a foil behind it.Â   -It works well for frosted and sea glass, almost as good as the pinterest picture. Very interesting combination!  - This project also works well for gems that have a 'rainbow' sheen on them, looks almost like the Arkenstone in The Hobbit trilogy.  So maybe it is a surface area thing, where more surface area = more crackles. I'll have to test my theory next time I do this. Hope this helped anyone who wants to try this!

ThreadBanger Rob, now this isn't exactly in a Pin or online, but here's something cool I did in my Chemistry Class last year.  You'll need two bowls, liquid soap, water, and straws. Put liquid soap in a bowl and put water and mix it up. Take the other bowl and just put water. Okay now dip one end of the straw in the soap water and blow it onto a table by putting the straw on the surface of the table. It may take a few tries but once you have a decent bubble, take anything and put it in the bowl of water and now you can put it in the bubble. Please Try it?

Hey, I'm a glass blowing artist so I think I can explain why the color marbles didn't make it. Colors cool the glass and make it harder to form when I'm in the shop. There are some colors that are cooler and some colors that are warmer but overall they still make the glass cooler than regular transparent glass. This also applies with your project. When you put them into the oven, the uncolored glass was able to take the heat better and stay intact and when you "shocked" them into the water, the colored glass cooled down and was unable to keep it's bond as one solid marble. I hope this makes sense.
